### [139] [Robust Localization for Autonomous Vehicles in Highway Scenes](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22040)
*Daqian Cheng,Xuchu Ding,Yujia Wu,Xiang Zhang,Lei Wang*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Robust highway localization using a dual-likelihood LiDAR front end and a Control-EKF, with automated high-cadence offline mapping and a public 163 km dataset; shows comparable urban performance to Apollo/Autoware and superior highway robustness, validated over 1M+ km.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Highway localization remains under-explored compared to urban scenes. Urban-centric methods degrade on highways due to environment homogeneity, occlusions, GNSS degradation, and stringent latency/accuracy demands. The paper seeks to close this gap by addressing highway-specific challenges.

Method: Introduce a dual-likelihood LiDAR front end that decouples 3D geometry from 2D road texture cues; employ a Control-EKF that fuses steering and acceleration commands to reduce lag; implement an automated offline mapping and ground-truth pipeline for high-cadence map refresh; release a public dataset (urban + highway, 163 km) with standardized product-oriented accuracy metrics and certified ground truth; benchmarking against Apollo and Autoware.

Result: The system achieves urban performance comparable to Apollo and Autoware, but demonstrates superior robustness on challenging highway scenarios; validated by over one million kilometers of road testing.

Conclusion: The proposed localization framework improves highway robustness and latency, with a data-centric contribution via a high-cadence map pipeline and public dataset to accelerate progress in the field.

Abstract: Localization for autonomous vehicles on highways remains under-explored compared to urban roads, and state-of-the-art methods for urban scenes degrade when directly applied to highways. We identify key challenges including environment changes under information homogeneity, heavy occlusion, degraded GNSS signals, and stringent downstream requirements on accuracy and latency. We propose a robust localization system to address highway challenges, which uses a dual-likelihood LiDAR front end that decouples 3D geometric structures and 2D road-texture cues to handle environment changes; a Control-EKF further leverages steering and acceleration commands to reduce lag and improve closed-loop behavior. An automated offline mapping and ground-truth pipeline keep maps fresh at high cadence for optimal localization performance. To catalyze progress, we release a public dataset covering both urban roads and highways while focusing on representative challenging highway clips, totaling 163 km; benchmarking is standardized using product-oriented accuracy metrics and certified ground truth. Compared to Apollo and Autoware, our system performs similarly on urban roads but shows superior robustness on challenging highway scenarios. The system has been validated by more than one million kilometers of road testing.

</details>


### [140] [SNGR: Selective Non-Gaussian Refinement for Ambiguous SLAM Factor Graphs](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22065)
*Anushka Kulkarni,Sarthak Dubey*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Selective non-Gaussian refinement (SNGR) augments iSAM2 with targeted nonlinear sampling on problematic windows to improve SLAM posteriors while reducing cost compared to exhaustive non-Gaussian inference.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Gaussian SLAM backends like iSAM2 can fail in regions with strong nonlinearity or data-association errors; a lightweight method is needed to detect and refine only the troublesome parts.

Method: Detect regions where Gaussian approximations fail by monitoring the condition number of joint marginal covariances; apply selective nested sampling using the full nonlinear factor graph likelihood on those windows; employ a gating mechanism to avoid degrading multimodal cases.

Result: In range-only SLAM with wrong data association, SNGR achieves high-precision failure detection and consistent local likelihood improvements, with reduced computational cost relative to exhaustive non-Gaussian inference.

Conclusion: Selective refinement shows promise for improving approximate SLAM posteriors, but its effectiveness depends on reliable region detection and gating; trade-offs between accuracy and computation remain.

Abstract: We present Selective Non-Gaussian Refinement (SNGR), a SLAM framework that augments iSAM2 with targeted nested sampling on windows where Gaussian approximations are likely to fail. We detect such regions using the condition number of joint marginal covariances and selectively refine them using the full nonlinear factor graph likelihood, with a gating mechanism to avoid degradation in multimodal cases. Experiments on range-only SLAM with wrong data association show that SNGR achieves high-precision failure detection and consistent local likelihood improvements while reducing computational cost relative to exhaustive non-Gaussian inference. These results highlight both the promise and the limitations of selective refinement for approximate SLAM posteriors.

</details>


### [141] [Wiggle and Go! System Identification for Zero-Shot Dynamic Rope Manipulation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22102)
*Arthur Jakobsson,Abhinav Mahajan,Karthik Pullalarevu,Krishna Suresh,Yunchao Yao,Yuemin Mao,Bardienus Duisterhof,Shahram Najam Syed,Jeffrey Ichnowski*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: A two-stage, system-identification framework for zero-shot dynamic rope manipulation that predicts rope physics to guide goal-conditioned actions, enabling efficient, accurate real-world execution across tasks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Dynamic rope manipulation is notoriously error-prone and data-hungry; there is a need for zero-shot, task-agnostic policies that generalize across rope tasks without large real-world datasets.

Method: A two-stage approach: (1) a system identification module observes rope movement to infer descriptive physical parameters; (2) an optimization-based planner uses these parameters to predict goal-conditioned robot actions, enabling zero-shot execution in the real world across multiple tasks.

Result: Demonstrates strong performance across dynamic rope tasks, with 3.55 cm average accuracy on 3D target striking using rope parameters (vs 15.34 cm without them), and a Pearson r=0.95 between predicted and real rope Fourier frequencies on an unseen trajectory, indicating faithful dynamic modeling.

Conclusion: A task-agnostic system-identification module enables a versatile policy that supports multiple dynamic rope manipulation tasks with zero-shot real-world execution and robust predictive fidelity.

Abstract: Many robotic tasks are unforgiving; a single mistake in a dynamic throw can lead to unacceptable delays or unrecoverable failure. To mitigate this, we present a novel approach that leverages learned simulation priors to inform goal-conditioned dynamic manipulation of ropes for efficient and accurate task execution. Related methods for dynamic rope manipulation either require large real-world datasets to estimate rope behavior or the use of iterative improvements on attempts at the task for goal completion. We introduce Wiggle and Go!, a system-identification, two-stage framework that enables zero-shot task rope manipulation. The framework consists of a system identification module that observes rope movement to predict descriptive physical parameters, which then informs an optimization method for goal-conditioned action prediction for the robot to execute zero-shot in the real. Our method achieves strong performance across multiple dynamic manipulation tasks enabled by the same task-agnostic system identification module which offers seamless switching between different manipulation tasks, allowing a single model to support a diverse array of manipulation policies. We achieve a 3.55 cm average accuracy on 3D target striking in real using rope system parameters in comparison to 15.34 cm accuracy when our task model is not system-parameter-informed. We achieve a Pearson correlation coefficient of 0.95 between Fourier frequencies of the predicted and real ropes on an unseen trajectory. Project website please see https://wiggleandgo.github.io/

</details>


### [142] [Dynamic Coupling and Indirect Control of Jointed Robots Rolling Atop A Moving Platform](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22104)
*Hamidreza Moradi,Scott David Kelly*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: An asymmetric two-link wheeled robot on a movable platform with no lateral slip can propel itself by internal joint actuation, producing fishlike undulatory locomotion. When two such robots share a common, inertially dynamic platform, their motions couple, affecting each other. The study develops a mathematical model and simulations, then shows that a single robot on a controlled platform can have its heading tracked by platform acceleration, enabling orbiting a fixed point on the platform or persistent directed locomotion.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand how internal actuation interacts with base/inertial dynamics to produce locomotion and coupling, and to explore control via base motion for steering and sustained motion in multi-robot and single-robot on-moving-base scenarios.

Method: Formulates a mathematical model (likely Lagrangian with nonholonomic/no-slip constraints) of an asymmetric two-link robot on a free-to-translate platform; analyzes system dynamics and coupling via simulations for two robots on a shared platform; then analyzes a single robot atop a controllable platform, showing how platform acceleration can steer heading and induce orbiting or persistent motion.

Result: 1) The two robots exhibit coupled dynamics through the shared platform, with locomotion of one influencing the other. 2) For a single robot on a platform driven by acceleration input, the robot's heading can be commanded to follow a desired time function, enabling orbiting around a fixed point and sustained directed locomotion.

Conclusion: Internal actuation combined with controlled platform dynamics suffices to induce and steer locomotion, including inter-robot coupling and precise heading tracking. This supports coordinated motion on shared baselines and programmable behaviors via base motion.

Abstract: An asymmetric two-link robot supported atop a flat platform by wheels that roll and pivot freely, but do not slip laterally, will develop forward momentum if the joint between the links is actuated internally. In particular, oscillations in the joint angle will generate undulatory locomotion suggesting fishlike swimming. If two such robots surmount a common platform that's free to translate with its own inertial dynamics, then the individual robots' dynamics will be coupled so that the locomotion of either robot is affected by that of the other. We develop a mathematical model for this system and present simulations demonstrating its behavior. We then consider a single robot with an unactuated joint rolling atop a platform that moves under control, and show that actuation of the platform is sufficient to dictate the robot's behavior. In particular, with the acceleration of the platform as an input, the robot's heading can be made to track a chosen function of time. This is sufficient to guarantee that the robot can be induced to orbit a fixed point on the platform or to locomote persistently in a desired direction.

</details>


### [143] [dWorldEval: Scalable Robotic Policy Evaluation via Discrete Diffusion World Model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22152)
*Yaxuan Li,Zhongyi Zhou,Yefei Chen,Yaokai Xue,Yichen Zhu*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Proposes dWorldEval, a discrete diffusion world model for scalable robotics policy evaluation that unifies vision, language, and actions into a single token space and uses a transformer-based denoising network with sparse keyframe memory and a progress token to predict future observations and task completion, outperforming prior methods on LIBERO, RoboTwin, and real-robot tasks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Evaluating robotics policies across thousands of environments and tasks is computationally intractable with existing approaches; a scalable evaluation proxy is needed.

Method: A discrete diffusion world model maps all modalities into a unified token space and denoises them with a single transformer network; employs a sparse keyframe memory to maintain spatiotemporal consistency; introduces a progress token to signal task completion; at inference, jointly predicts future observations and progress token to automatically determine success when progress reaches 1.

Result: Extensive experiments show dWorldEval significantly outperforms WorldEval, Ctrl-World, and WorldGym on LIBERO, RoboTwin, and multiple real-robot tasks.

Conclusion: Presents a new architectural paradigm for scalable robotics world simulators aimed at evaluating policies at scale; demonstrates strong empirical performance and potential for broad adoption.

Abstract: Evaluating robotics policies across thousands of environments and thousands of tasks is infeasible with existing approaches. This motivates the need for a new methodology for scalable robotics policy evaluation. In this paper, we propose dWorldEval, which uses a discrete diffusion world model as a scalable evaluation proxy for robotics policies. Specifically, dWorldEval maps all modalities - including vision, language, and robotic actions - into a unified token space, modeling them via a single transformer-based denoising network. In this paper, we propose dWorldEval, using a discrete diffusion world model as a scalable evaluation proxy for robotics policy. Specifically, it maps all modalities, including vision, language, and robotics action into a unified token space, then denoises them with a single transformer network. Building on this architecture, we employ a sparse keyframe memory to maintain spatiotemporal consistency. We also introduce a progress token that indicates the degree of task completion. At inference, the model jointly predicts future observations and progress token, allowing automatically determine success when the progress reaches 1. Extensive experiments demonstrate that dWorldEval significantly outperforms previous approaches, i.e., WorldEval, Ctrl-World, and WorldGym, on LIBERO, RoboTwin, and multiple real-robot tasks. It paves the way for a new architectural paradigm in building world simulators for robotics evaluation at scale.

</details>


### [144] [Energy-Efficient Multi-Robot Coverage Path Planning of Non-Convex Regions of Interests](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22189)
*Sourav Raxit,Jose Fuentes,Paulo Padrao,Abdullah Al Redwan Newaz,Md Tamjidul Hoque,Mark Kulp,Leonardo Bobadilla*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: A multi-robot coverage path planning framework (MRCPP) for large, nonconvex regions with obstacles and NFZs, achieving energy efficiency and cross-platform applicability. It uses global swath generation, parallel sweeps with minimal turns, safety buffers, an mTSP solver for workload balance, and a modified visibility graph with heading tracking. Demonstrated on AAVs and ASVs, it outperforms state-of-the-art planners in energy (3-40% for 3 robots) and computation time (×10), with open-source release.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing energy-efficient coverage planners rely on boustrophedon decomposition and do not guarantee optimal energy efficiency; most frameworks support only a single robotic platform. There is a need for energy-efficient, scalable, cross-platform multi-robot CPP in complex environments.

Method: 1) Globally-informed swath pattern generation. 2) Parallel sweeping paths with minimal turns. 3) Safety buffer computation for turning clearance. 4) Efficient mTSP solver to balance workloads and minimize mission time. 5) Connect disjoint segments via a modified visibility graph that tracks heading angles while ensuring transitions occur in safe regions.

Result: Real-world experiments with autonomous aerial vehicles (AAVs) and autonomous surface vehicles (ASVs) show consistent improvement over state-of-the-art planners in energy efficiency and computation time. Quantitatively, average total energy consumption reduced by 3% to 40% for a 3-robot team; computation time reduced by an order of magnitude. Workload distribution remains balanced and scalability improves with fleet size. Open-source release and demonstration videos available at the project site.

Conclusion: MRCPP provides a scalable, cross-platform, energy-efficient multi-robot CPP framework that outperforms current planners and is available as an open-source package.

Abstract: This letter presents an energy-efficient multi-robot coverage path planning (MRCPP) framework for large, nonconvex Regions of Interest (ROI) containing obstacles and no-fly zones (NFZ). Existing minimum-energy coverage planning algorithms utilize meta-heuristic boustrophedon workspace decomposition. Therefore, even with minimum energy objectives and energy consumption constraints, they cannot achieve optimal energy efficiency. Moreover, most existing frameworks support only a single type of robotic platform. MRCPP overcomes these limitations by: generating globally-informed swath generation, creating parallel sweeping paths with minimal turns, calculating safety buffers to ensure safe turning clearance, using an efficient mTSP solver to balance workloads and minimize mission time, and connecting disjoint segments via a modified visibility graph that tracks heading angles while maintaining transitions within safe regions. The efficacy of the proposed MRCPP framework is demonstrated through real-world experiments involving autonomous aerial vehicles (AAVs) and autonomous surface vehicles (ASVs). Evaluations demonstrate that the proposed MRCPP consistently outperforms state-of-the-art planners, reducing average total energy consumption by 3\% to 40\% for a team of 3 robots and computation time by an order of magnitude, while maintaining balanced workload distribution and strong scalability across increasing fleet sizes. The MRCPP framework is released as an open-source package and videos of real-world and simulated experiments are available at https://mrc-pp.github.io.

</details>


### [145] [V-STC: A Time-Efficient Multi-Vehicle Coordinated Trajectory Planning Approach](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22196)
*Pengfei Liu,Jialing Zhou,Yuezu Lv,Guanghui Wen,Tingwen Huang*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Proposes variable-time-step spatio-temporal corridors (V-STC) for multi-vehicle coordination to improve temporal efficiency while ensuring safety; optimizes per-vehicle corridors with variable spatial cuboids and durations; results in faster, collision-free trajectories compared with fixed-time STCs.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Address inefficiency in multi-AV coordination due to rigid, fixed-time-step corridors by enabling flexible timing and positioning to reduce temporal occupancy.

Method: Formulate an optimization to construct a V-STC for each vehicle, with decision variables for corridor spatial configuration (cube positions) and their time durations; ensure spatio-temporal collision avoidance; plan dynamically feasible trajectories per vehicle from the V-STC.

Result: Simulation studies show safe coordination and improved time efficiency relative to existing STC methods.

Conclusion: V-STC increases temporal efficiency in multi-vehicle coordination while maintaining safety, enabling per-vehicle independent trajectory planning.

Abstract: Coordinating the motions of multiple autonomous vehicles (AVs) requires planning frameworks that ensure safety while making efficient use of space and time. This paper presents a new approach, termed variable-time-step spatio-temporal corridor (V-STC), that enhances the temporal efficiency of multi-vehicle coordination. An optimization model is formulated to construct a V-STC for each AV, in which both the spatial configuration of the corridor cubes and their time durations are treated as decision variables. By allowing the corridor's spatial position and time step to vary, the constructed V-STC reduces the overall temporal occupancy of each AV while maintaining collision-free separation in the spatio-temporal domain. Based on the generated V-STC, a dynamically feasible trajectory is then planned independently for each AV. Simulation studies demonstrate that the proposed method achieves safe multi-vehicle coordination and yields more time-efficient motion compared with existing STC approaches.

### [146] [An LLM-Driven Closed-Loop Autonomous Learning Framework for Robots Facing Uncovered Tasks in Open Environments](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22199)
*Hong Su*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: An LLM-driven closed-loop autonomous learning framework enables robots to convert execution and observation experiences into reusable local methods, reducing dependence on external LLMs and improving efficiency.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing robotic systems rely heavily on predefined methods and repeated LLM interactions for uncovered tasks; need for autonomous, self-improving local knowledge.

Method: Retrieve local method library; if absent, use LLM as high-level reasoner for task analysis, model selection, data collection planning, and strategy; learn from self-execution and active observation; quasi-real-time training; consolidate validated results into library.

Result: Shows reduced execution time and reduced LLM calls: e.g., total execution time from 7.7772s to 6.7779s; LLM calls per task from 1.0 to 0.2.

Conclusion: Framework enables gradual conversion of experience into reusable local capabilities and reduces future reliance on external LLMs.

Abstract: Autonomous robots operating in open environments need the ability to continuously handle tasks that are not covered by predefined local methods. However, existing approaches often rely on repeated large-language-model (LLM) interaction for uncovered tasks, and even successful executions or observed successful external behaviors are not always autonomously transformed into reusable local knowledge. In this paper, we propose an LLM-driven closed-loop autonomous learning framework for robots facing uncovered tasks in open environments. The proposed framework first retrieves the local method library to determine whether a reusable solution already exists for the current task or observed event. If no suitable method is found, it triggers an autonomous learning process in which the LLM serves as a high-level reasoning component for task analysis, candidate model selection, data collection planning, and execution or observation strategy organization. The robot then learns from both self-execution and active observation, performs quasi-real-time training and adjustment, and consolidates the validated result into the local method library for future reuse. Through this recurring closed-loop process, the robot gradually converts both execution-derived and observation-derived experience into reusable local capability while reducing future dependence on repeated external LLM interaction. Results show that the proposed framework reduces execution time and LLM dependence in both repeated-task self-execution and observation-driven settings, for example reducing the average total execution time from 7.7772s to 6.7779s and the average number of LLM calls per task from 1.0 to 0.2 in the repeated-task self-execution experiments.

</details>


### [147] [Learning-augmented robotic automation for real-world manufacturing](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22235)

Abstract: Industrial robots are widely used in manufacturing, yet most manipulation still depends on fixed waypoint scripts that are brittle to environmental changes. It maintained near-human takt time while reducing variability in solder-joint quality and cycle time. These results establish a practical pathway for extending industrial automation with learning-based methods.

### [148] [CodeGraphVLP: Code-as-Planner Meets Semantic-Graph State for Non-Markovian Vision-Language-Action Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22238)
*Khoa Vo,Sieu Tran,Taisei Hanyu,Yuki Ikebe,Duy Nguyen,Bui Duy Quoc Nghi,Minh Vu,Anthony Gunderman,Chase Rainwater,Anh Nguyen,Ngan Le*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: CodeGraphVLP presents a hierarchical framework that maintains a persistent semantic-graph state, uses an executable code-based planner with progress checks, and applies progress-guided visual-language prompting to enable reliable long-horizon manipulation under partial observability and clutter, outperforming strong VLA baselines with reduced planning latency.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Vision-Language-Action models struggle with long-horizon, non-Markovian tasks where relevant evidence can be occluded or appear earlier in trajectories; cluttered scenes make fine-grained grounding brittle, necessitating persistent representations and efficient planning.

Method: Introduce CodeGraphVLP, a hierarchical system combining a persistent semantic-graph state with a code-based planner that operates on the graph to perform progress checks and emit subtask instructions and relevant objects. These outputs generate clutter-suppressed observations for a VLA executor; progress-guided prompting further focuses visual-language reasoning. Ablations validate each component.

Result: On real-world non-Markovian tasks, CodeGraphVLP improves task completion over strong VLA baselines and history-enabled variants and reduces planning latency compared to VLM-in-the-loop planning; extensive ablations confirm contributions of each component.

Conclusion: A persistent semantic-graph plus executable planning and progress-guided prompting yields robust long-horizon manipulation in partially observable, cluttered environments, with improved efficiency and clear contributions demonstrated via ablations.

Abstract: Vision-Language-Action (VLA) models promise generalist robot manipulation, but are typically trained and deployed as short-horizon policies that assume the latest observation is sufficient for action reasoning. This assumption breaks in non-Markovian long-horizon tasks, where task-relevant evidence can be occluded or appear only earlier in the trajectory, and where clutter and distractors make fine-grained visual grounding brittle. We present CodeGraphVLP, a hierarchical framework that enables reliable long-horizon manipulation by combining a persistent semantic-graph state with an executable code-based planner and progress-guided visual-language prompting. The semantic-graph maintains task-relevant entities and relations under partial observability. The synthesized planner executes over this semantic-graph to perform efficient progress checks and outputs a subtask instruction together with subtask-relevant objects. We use these outputs to construct clutter-suppressed observations that focus the VLA executor on critical evidence. On real-world non-Markovian tasks, CodeGraphVLP improves task completion over strong VLA baselines and history-enabled variants while substantially lowering planning latency compared to VLM-in-the-loop planning. ### [149] [Learning Control Policies to Provably Satisfy Hard Affine Constraints for Black-Box Hybrid Dynamical Systems](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22244)
*Aayushi Shrivastava,Kartik Nagpal,Sairam Jinkala,Jean-Baptiste Bouvier,Negar Mehr*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: A safe RL framework for black-box hybrid dynamics with affine resets, enforcing an affine policy with boundary- and pre-reset repulsion to guarantee constraint satisfaction in closed-loop, outperforming reward shaping and learned-CBF baselines on constrained pendulum and paddle juggler tasks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To provide provable safety guarantees for reinforcement learning in hybrid systems that exhibit instantaneous state jumps and unknown nonlinear dynamics, where traditional CBFs and RL safety approaches rely on known models.

Method: Restrict the RL policy to be affine in the state and engineer two repulsive affine regions: one near constraint boundaries to prevent violations under unknown dynamics, and a second before resets to prevent post-reset constraint violations due to impact. Derive sufficient conditions ensuring closed-loop safety; compare with reward shaping and learned-CBF baselines on hybrid tasks.

Result: Derives sufficient conditions under which the affine, repulsive-policy guarantees constraint satisfaction in closed loop. Empirical results show always-safe operation and higher policy quality than baselines on the constrained pendulum and paddle juggler.

Abstract: Ensuring safety for black-box hybrid dynamical systems presents significant challenges due to their instantaneous state jumps and unknown explicit nonlinear dynamics. Existing solutions for strict safety constraint satisfaction, like control barrier functions (CBFs) and reachability analysis, rely on direct knowledge of the dynamics. Similarly, safe reinforcement learning (RL) approaches often rely on known system dynamics or merely discourage safety violations through reward shaping. In this work, we want to learn RL policies which provably satisfy affine state constraints in closed loop for black-box hybrid dynamical systems with affine reset maps. Our key insight is forcing the RL policy to be affine and repulsive near the constraint boundaries for the unknown nonlinear dynamics of the system, providing guarantees that the trajectories will not violate the constraint. We further account for constraint violation due to instantaneous state jumps that occur due to impacts or reset maps in the hybrid system by introducing a second repulsive affine region before the reset that prevents post-reset states from violating the constraint. We derive sufficient conditions under which these policies satisfy safety constraints in closed loop. We also compare our approach with state-of-the-art reward shaping and learned-CBF methods on hybrid dynamical systems like the constrained pendulum and paddle juggler environments. In both scenarios, we show that our methodology learns higher quality policies while always satisfying the safety constraints.

### [150] [False Feasibility in Variable Impedance MPC for Legged Locomotion](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22251)
*Vishal Ramesh*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: MPC with stiffness as an instantaneous decision variable expands the feasible set beyond what actuator dynamics can realize. There is a formal mismatch between the parameter-based feasible set Fparam and the true realizable set Freal, governed by alpha = omega_s T. In a 1D hopping monoped, there exists a closed-form alpha_crit below which no admissible stiffness command can realize the parameter-based prediction; numerical results confirm monotonic deviation as alpha decreases with near-perfect scaling. Transferring to planar SLIP dynamics, the primary consequences are COM and stance-timing deviations, with regime-dependent friction effects. A second threshold alpha_infeas < alpha_crit defines a floor where restricting stiffness cannot repair realizability. Augmenting the prediction state with stiffness removes the mismatch by construction; thus, stiffness-aware MPC offers a conservative-tuning remedy rather than relying on aggressive decoupling. 


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To diagnose and resolve a fundamental modeling vs. actuation limitation in variable-impedance MPC for legged locomotion, where treating stiffness as a free optimization variable yields predictions that may be physically unrealizable under real actuator dynamics.

Method: Derive a formal distinction between parameter-based feasible set Fparam and realizable set Freal. Introduce dimensionless alpha = omega_s T to capture the actuator bandwidth relative to task timescale. Prove, in 1D hopping monoped, the existence of alpha_crit with a closed-form expression from task physics such that for alpha < alpha_crit no stiffness command can satisfy parameter-based predictions. Validate numerically over ten parameter combinations showing robust scaling (log-log R^2 ≈ 0.99). Transfer the mechanism to planar SLIP dynamics to identify center-of-mass and stance-timing deviations as primary effects and friction as a tertiary observable. Establish alpha_infeas < alpha_crit as a floor below which restricting stiffness cannot ensure realizability. Propose augmenting the prediction state with stiffness to close the mismatch by construction.

Result: Analytical threshold alpha_crit demarcates realizability; below it, parameter-based MPC predictions are unattainable; numerical validation supports the scaling; 2D SLIP transfer reveals primary kinematic effects; a second threshold alpha_infeas defines a limit to repair via conservative tuning; stiffness-augmented predictions remove mismatch by construction.

Conclusion: The mismatch is structural, not merely a modeling approximation. Incorporating stiffness as part of the prediction state resolves the discrepancy between MPC predictions and actuators, ensuring realizability and enabling conservative tuning of variable-impedance controllers.

Abstract: Variable impedance model predictive control (MPC) formulations that treat joint stiffness as an instantaneous decision variable operate on a feasible set strictly larger than the physically realizable set under first-order actuator dynamics. We identify this as a formulation error rather than a modeling approximation, formalize the distinction between the parameter-based feasible set Fparam and the realizable set Freal, and characterize the regime of mismatch via the dimensionless parameter alpha = omega_sT (actuator bandwidth times task timescale). For the 1D hopping monoped, we prove that below an analytical threshold alpha_crit derived in closed form from task physics, no admissible stiffness command realizes the parameter-based prediction. Numerical validation in 1D shows monotonic deviation growth as alpha decreases, with the predicted scaling holding across ten parameter combinations (log-log R2 = 0.99). Mechanism transfer to planar spring-loaded inverted pendulum dynamics confirms center-of-mass and stance-timing deviation as the primary consequence, with regime-dependent friction effects as a tertiary observable. A second threshold alpha_infeas < alpha_crit establishes a floor below which restricting the admissible stiffness range cannot repair realizability, closing the conservative-tuning objection on structural grounds. Augmenting the prediction state with stiffness closes the mismatch by construction.

### [151] [A Kinematic Analysis of Palm Degrees of Freedom for Enhancing Thumb Opposability in Robotic Hands](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22283)
*HyoJae Kang,Yeong Jae Park,Hyunmok Jung,Joonho Lee,Dong Il Park*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Palm degrees of freedom (DoF) in a five-finger robotic hand substantially enhance thumb opposability by repositioning finger bases via palm motion; when total DoF is constrained, redistributing DoF to the palm trades workspace expansion against kinematic redundancy; results support joint design consideration of palm and finger DoF.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Quantify the kinematic role of palm DoF in thumb opposability and provide design guidelines independent of object/contact models.

Method: A five-finger hand model with a five-DoF thumb and four fingers (3–4 DoF each). Palm motion is allowed between adjacent fingers. Overlap workspace volume is defined from voxelized fingertip reachable regions. Seven design cases include increasing total DoF and redistributing DoF from fingers to the palm.

Result: Palm DoF significantly improves opposability, especially for the ring and little fingers, by repositioning base locations rather than merely extending reach. When total DoF is constrained, moving DoF to the palm creates trade-offs between overlap-space expansion and kinematic redundancy. Palm and finger DoF play distinct, complementary roles.

Abstract: This study investigates the kinematic role of palm degrees of freedom (DoF) in enhancing thumb opposability in a five-finger robotic hand. A hand model consisting of a five DoF thumb and four fingers with three to four DoF is analyzed, where palm motion is introduced between adjacent fingers. To quantitatively evaluate thumb-finger interaction, the overlap workspace volume is defined based on voxelized fingertip reachable regions. Seven cases are considered, including configurations with increased total DoF and configurations in which the total DoF is maintained by redistributing DoF from the fingers to the palm. The results show that palm DoF significantly improves opposability, particularly for the ring and little fingers, by repositioning their base locations rather than simply extending their reachable range. However, when the total DoF is constrained, redistributing DoF to the palm leads to trade-offs between overlap workspace expansion and kinematic redundancy. These findings indicate that palm DoF and finger DoF play distinct roles in hand kinematics and should be considered jointly in design. This study provides a quantitative framework for evaluating palm-induced opposability without relying on object or contact models and offers practical design guidelines for incorporating palm motion in robotic hands.

Specifically, it identifies critical interaction regions from benign trajectories and positions the risk factor within these regions, aiming to entangle it with the VLA's execution flow and elicit a target unsafe behavior. (II) \textbf{Risk Amplification} ensures stable elicitation across heterogeneous models. It iteratively refines the risk factor state through gradient-free optimization guided by trajectory features. Experiments on six representative VLA models show that RedVLA uncovers diverse unsafe behaviors and achieves the ASR up to 95.5\% within 10 optimization iterations. ### [158] [ATRS: Adaptive Trajectory Re-splitting via a Shared Neural Policy for Parallel Optimization](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22715)
*Jiajun Yu,Guodong Liu,Li Wang,Pengxiang Zhou,Wentao Liu,Yin He,Chao Xu,Fei Gao,Yanjun Cao*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: ATRS uses a shared-policy DRL to adaptively re-split parallel ADMM trajectory optimization, improving convergence speed and real-time performance.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Fixed-structure parallel ADMM can stagnate in highly constrained regions; online adaptive re-splitting is needed to ensure robust convergence.

Method: Formulate adaptive re-splitting as a Multi-Agent Shared-Policy MDP with homogeneous trajectory-segment agents sharing a single neural policy; the approach is size-invariant and supports zero-shot generalization. A Confidence-Based Election selects the most stagnating segment for re-splitting at each step.

Result: Convergence is accelerated: iterations reduced by up to 26.0% and computation time by up to 19.1%. Real-world tests show applicability to large-scale offline global planning and real-time onboard replanning at ~35 ms per cycle, with no sim-to-real degradation.

Conclusion: Integrating a shared DRL policy into ADMM yields a scalable, generalizable adaptive parallel optimization framework for long-horizon trajectory planning, capable of handling varying segment counts and unseen environments.

Abstract: Parallel trajectory optimization via the Alternating Direction Method of Multipliers (ADMM) has emerged as a scalable approach to long-horizon motion planning. However, existing frameworks typically decompose the problem into parallel subproblems based on a predefined fixed structure. Such structural rigidity often causes optimization stagnation in highly constrained regions, where a few lagging subproblems delay global convergence. A natural remedy is to adaptively re-split these stagnating segments online. Yet, deciding when, where, and how to split exceeds the capability of rule-based heuristics. To this end, we propose ATRS, a novel framework that embeds a shared Deep Reinforcement Learning policy into the parallel ADMM loop. We formulate this adaptive adjustment as a Multi-Agent Shared-Policy Markov Decision Process, where all trajectory segments act as homogeneous agents and share a unified neural policy network. This parameter-sharing architecture endows the system with size invariance, enabling it to handle dynamically changing segment counts during re-splitting and generalize to arbitrary trajectory lengths. Furthermore, our formulation inherently supports zero-shot generalization to unseen environments, as our network relies solely on the internal states of the numerical solver rather than on the geometric features of the environment. To ensure solver stability, a Confidence-Based Election mechanism selects only the most stagnating segment for re-splitting at each step. Extensive simulations demonstrate that ATRS accelerates convergence, reducing the number of iterations by up to 26.0% and the computation time by up to 19.1%. Real-world experiments further confirm its applicability to both large-scale offline global planning and real-time onboard replanning within 35 ms per cycle, with no sim-to-real degradation.

### [159] [GCImOpt: Learning efficient goal-conditioned policies by imitating optimal trajectories](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22724)

Method: Generate large datasets by efficient trajectory optimization to produce thousands of optimal trajectories. Augment data by treating intermediate states as goals to increase dataset size by an order of magnitude. Train goal-conditioned neural networks to steer the system toward arbitrary goals.

Abstract: Imitation learning is a well-established approach for machine-learning-based control. However, its applicability depends on having access to demonstrations, which are often expensive to collect and/or suboptimal for solving the task. In this work, we present GCImOpt, an approach to learn efficient goal-conditioned policies by training on datasets generated by trajectory optimization. Our approach for dataset generation is computationally efficient, can generate thousands of optimal trajectories in minutes on a laptop computer, and produces high-quality demonstrations. Further, by means of a data augmentation scheme that treats intermediate states as goals, we are able to increase the training dataset size by an order of magnitude. Using our generated datasets, we train goal-conditioned neural network policies that can control the system towards arbitrary goals. To demonstrate the generality of our approach, we generate datasets and then train policies for various control tasks, namely cart-pole stabilization, planar and three-dimensional quadcopter stabilization, and point reaching using a 6-DoF robot arm. We show that our trained policies can achieve high success rates and near-optimal control profiles, all while being small (less than 80,000 neural network parameters) and fast enough (up to more than 6,000 times faster than a trajectory optimization solver) that they could be deployed onboard resource-constrained controllers. We provide videos, code, datasets and pre-trained policies under a free software license; see our project website https://jongoiko.github.io/gcimopt/.

</details>


<div id='cs.CG'></div>

# cs.CG [[Back]](#toc)

### [160] [Counting All Lattice Rectangles in the Square Grid in Near-Linear Time](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.22456)
*Dmitry Babichev,Sergey Babichev*

Main category: cs.CG

TL;DR: Presents exact counting algorithms for lattice rectangles in [0,n)^2 (including non-axis-aligned) with progressively improved complexities down to O(n log^3 n); uses param by primitive direction and side lengths; reduces to weighted floor sums with affine/reciprocal invariance; also derives a two-term asymptotic expansion F(n) ~ c n^4 log n + B n^4, providing a consistency check.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Resolve the exact counting problem for lattice rectangles, a fundamental combinatorial and geometric enumeration task, and push toward near-linear-time exact algorithms; also supply asymptotic expansion to validate numerical experiments.

Method: Parametrize rectangles by primitive direction (u,v) and two side lengths; transform the counting into a constant-size family of weighted floor sums closed under affine and reciprocal transformations; enable O(log n) evaluation per query, yielding total complexities O(n^2), O(n^{3/2} log n), O(n^{4/3} log n), and O(n log^3 n) across algorithmic variants; derive two-term asymptotics via analytic summation.

Result: A sequence of exact algorithms with decreasing time complexity culminating in near-linear time O(n log^3 n); explicit two-term asymptotic expansion F(n) = ((4 log 2 - 1)/π^2) n^4 log n + B n^4 + o(n^4), with B given explicitly; consistency check for large-n numerics.

Conclusion: Demonstrates that exact counting of lattice rectangles within a square can be done in near-linear time and that the asymptotic expansion provides a robust cross-check; methodology may adapt to related lattice polygon counting problems and higher-dimensional analogues.

Abstract: We study the exact counting problem for all lattice rectangles contained in the square $[0,n)\times[0,n)$, including non-axis-parallel ones. Starting from the standard parametrization by a primitive direction $(u,v)$ and two side lengths, we derive a sequence of exact algorithms of complexity $O(n^2)$, $O(n^{3/2}\log n)$, $O(n^{4/3}\log n)$, and finally $O(n\log^3 n)$. The main idea behind the near-linear algorithm is to reduce the geometric summation to a constant-size family of weighted floor sums closed under Euclidean-style affine and reciprocal transformations, and hence evaluable in $O(\log n)$ time per query. Besides the exact algorithmic result, we also derive a two-term asymptotic expansion, $F(n)=\frac{4\log 2-1}{π^2}n^4\log n+B\,n^4+o(n^4)$ with the explicit formula for $B$, which provides an independent consistency check for the large-$n$ numerical data produced by the algorithms.

</details>
